<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Painting</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Practice of applying paint, pigment, color or other medium to a surface</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about artistic painting. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Painting_(disambiguation)" title="Painting (disambiguation)">Painting (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Painter" redirects here. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Painter_(disambiguation)" title="Painter (disambiguation)">Painter (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mona_Lisa,_by_Leonardo_da_Vinci,_from_C2RMF_retouched.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="11146" data-file-width="7479" decoding="async" height="328" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Mona_Lisa%2C_by_Leonardo_da_Vinci%2C_from_C2RMF_retouched.jpg/220px-Mona_Lisa%2C_by_Leonardo_da_Vinci%2C_from_C2RMF_retouched.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Mona_Lisa%2C_by_Leonardo_da_Vinci%2C_from_C2RMF_retouched.jpg/330px-Mona_Lisa%2C_by_Leonardo_da_Vinci%2C_from_C2RMF_retouched.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Mona_Lisa%2C_by_Leonardo_da_Vinci%2C_from_C2RMF_retouched.jpg/440px-Mona_Lisa%2C_by_Leonardo_da_Vinci%2C_from_C2RMF_retouched.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mona_Lisa,_by_Leonardo_da_Vinci,_from_C2RMF_retouched.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <i><a href="/wiki/Mona_Lisa" title="Mona Lisa">Mona Lisa</a></i> (1503–1517) by <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">Leonardo da Vinci</a> is one of the world's most recognizable paintings.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rhinos_Chauvet_Cave.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1366" decoding="async" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Rhinos_Chauvet_Cave.jpg/400px-Rhinos_Chauvet_Cave.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Rhinos_Chauvet_Cave.jpg/600px-Rhinos_Chauvet_Cave.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Rhinos_Chauvet_Cave.jpg/800px-Rhinos_Chauvet_Cave.jpg 2x" width="400"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rhinos_Chauvet_Cave.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An artistic depiction of a group of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhino" title="Rhino">rhinos</a> was made in the <a href="/wiki/Chauvet_Cave" title="Chauvet Cave">Chauvet Cave</a> 30,000 to 32,000 years ago.</div></div></div>
<p><b>Painting</b> is the practice of applying <a href="/wiki/Paint" title="Paint">paint</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pigment" title="Pigment">pigment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Color" title="Color">color</a> or other medium to a solid surface (called the "matrix" or "support").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> The medium is commonly applied to the base with a <a href="/wiki/Brush" title="Brush">brush</a>, but other implements, such as knives, sponges, and <a href="/wiki/Airbrush" title="Airbrush">airbrushes</a>, can be used.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Art" title="Art">art</a>, the term <i>painting </i>describes both the act and the result of the action (the final work is called "a painting"). The support for paintings includes such surfaces as walls, paper, canvas, wood, glass, <a href="/wiki/Lacquer" title="Lacquer">lacquer</a>, pottery, <a href="/wiki/Leaf" title="Leaf">leaf</a>, copper and <a href="/wiki/Concrete" title="Concrete">concrete</a>, and the painting may incorporate multiple other materials, including sand, <a href="/wiki/Clay" title="Clay">clay</a>, paper, <a href="/wiki/Plaster" title="Plaster">plaster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gold_leaf" title="Gold leaf">gold leaf</a>, and even whole objects.
</p><p>Painting is an important form in the <a href="/wiki/Visual_arts" title="Visual arts">visual arts</a>, bringing in elements such as <a href="/wiki/Drawing" title="Drawing">drawing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Composition_(visual_arts)" title="Composition (visual arts)">composition</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gesture" title="Gesture">gesture</a> (as in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gestural_painting" title="Gestural painting">gestural painting</a>), <a href="/wiki/Narrative" title="Narrative">narration</a> (as in <a href="/wiki/Narrative_art" title="Narrative art">narrative art</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Abstraction" title="Abstraction">abstraction</a> (as in <a href="/wiki/Abstract_art" title="Abstract art">abstract art</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> Paintings can be naturalistic and representational (as in <a href="/wiki/Still_life" title="Still life">still life</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landscape_art" title="Landscape art">landscape painting</a>), <a href="/wiki/Photorealism" title="Photorealism">photographic</a>, abstract, narrative, <a href="/wiki/Symbol" title="Symbol">symbolistic</a> (as in <a href="/wiki/Symbolism_(arts)" title="Symbolism (arts)">Symbolist art</a>), <a href="/wiki/Emotion" title="Emotion">emotive</a> (as in <a href="/wiki/Expressionism" title="Expressionism">Expressionism</a>) or <a href="/wiki/Politics" title="Politics">political</a> in nature (as in <a href="/wiki/Artivism" title="Artivism">Artivism</a>).
</p><p>A portion of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_painting" title="History of painting">history of painting</a> in both Eastern and Western art is dominated by <a href="/wiki/Religious_art" title="Religious art">religious art</a>. Examples of this kind of painting range from artwork depicting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mythology" title="Mythology">mythological</a> figures on pottery, to <a href="/wiki/Bible" title="Bible">Biblical</a> scenes on the <a href="/wiki/Sistine_Chapel_ceiling" title="Sistine Chapel ceiling">Sistine Chapel ceiling</a>, to scenes from the life of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_painting" title="Chinese painting">Buddha</a> (or other images of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_art_history" title="Eastern art history">Eastern religious origin</a>).
</p>
